TABLE I
ATABLEARAN
OF
THE TITLES OF THE PUBLIC GENERAL ACTS
OF 1927
being the Acts passed in the THIRD SESSION of the
SECOND PARLIAMENT OF NORTHERN IRELAND .
17 GEO . 5.-A.D. 1927 .
17 & 18 GEO . 5.-A.D. 1927 .
17 GEO . 5 .
1. An Act to confirm and give effectto an agreement relatingto
the establishmentof an AgriculturalResearch Station for
Northern Ireland, and to incorporatecertainTrusteesfor the
controland management of the said Station,and for purposes
connected therewith. (AgriculturalResearchStation.)
2. An Act to apply certainSums out of the ConsolidatedFund of
Northern Irelandto the serviceof the years ending on the
thirty-firstday of March , nineteenhundred and twenty-seven,
and the thirty-firstday of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-
eight. (Consolidated Fund .)
3.An Act to amend the law relatingto injuryto certainclassesof
livestock by dogs. (Dogs.)
4. An Act to amend the Labourers Act (Northern Ireland), 1923,
in its applicationto certainloans and advances under the
Labourers Acts (Northern Ireland), 1883 to 1923. (Labourers'
Cottages(Loans).)
5. An Act to alterthe allocationofcertainsalarieswhich arepayable
under theSalariesofMinisterialOfficesAct,1921 [N.I.] (Salaries
of MinisterialOffices.)

## Page 4

iv. [17 & 18 GEO . 5.]Table of the Statutes.
17 & 18 GEO . 5.
6. An Act to regulatethe saleon commission ofhorticulturalproduce.
(HorticulturalProduce (Saleson Commission).)
7. An Act to make betterprovisionfor the protectionagainstlead
poisoning of persons employed in painting buildings. (Lead
Paint (ProtectionagainstPoisoning).)
8. An Act to amend the Loans Guarantee Acts (Northern Ireland),
1922 to 1926,by increasingthe amount of loanswhich may be
guaranteed under the said Acts. (Loans Guarantee.)
9. An Act to empower railwaycompanies to provide and run road
vehicles. (Railways (Road Vehicles).)
10. An Act to make furtherprovisionfor the bringingintoaccount
ofthe Northern Irelandresiduaryshareofreservedtaxes,and for
payments to the reservefund,and to chargeon the Consolidated
Fund certainsums forthe purposesof agricultureand housing.
(Exchequer and FinancialProvisions.)
11. An Act to alterthe Rate of Entertainments Duty ,to amend the
Law relatingto certainDuties of Inland Revenue (including
Excise),and to make provisionfor Reliefin respectof Double
Taxation as between Northern Ireland and Great Britain and
as between Northern Irelandand the IrishFree State,and for
purposes connected therewith. (Finance.)
12. An Act to apply a Sum out of the ConsolidatedFund ofNorthern
Irelandto the serviceof the year ending on the thirty-firstday
ofMarch ,nineteenhundred and twenty-eight,and to appropriate
the Suppliesgranted in thisSessionof Parliament. (Appropri-
ation.)
13. An Act to amend the provisionsof the Workmen's Compensation
Acts (Northern Ireland), 1906 to 1923 ; and to give effectin
Northern Ireland to certain enactments of the Workmen's
Compensation Act , 1925. (Workmen's Compensation (Mis-
cellaneousAmendments ).) [Repealed by Chapter 16.]
14. An Act to continuecertainExpiring Laws as respectsNorthern
Ireland. (Expiring Laws Continuance.)
15. An Act to amend sectionone of the Housing Act (Northern
Ireland), 1923, as amended by subsequent enactments, and to
extend the powers of localauthoritiesin connection with the
sale of houses. (Housing.)

## Page 5

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] Table of the Statutes. V.
16.An Act to consolidate, as respectNorthern Ireland, the law
relatingto compensation to workmen for injuriessufferedin
the course of theiremployment . (Workmen's Compensation).
17. An Act to provide for the granting of licencesfor the sale of
milk under specialdesignations. (Sale of Milk .)
18. An Act to amend the provisionsofthe Rent and Mortgage Interest
(Restrictions)Acts(NorthernIreland),1920to1925,withrespect
to houses letwith furnitureand the obtainingof possessionof
houses by misrepresentation. (Rent and Mortgage Interest
Restrictions, Amendment .)
19.An Act to consolidate,with amendments ,the enactments relating
to quarries,and forpurposesconnectedtherewith. (Quarries.)
20. An Act to declareand amend the law relatingto tradedisputes
and trade unions,to regulatethe positionof civilservantsand
personsemployedby publicauthoritiesinrespectofmembership
of tradeunionsand similarorganisations,to extend sectionfive
ofthe Conspiracy,and Protectionof PropertyAct,1875,and for
other purposes connected with the purposes aforesaid. (Trade
Disputes and Trade Unions.)
21. An Act to amend the law relatingto the saleand supply of intoxi-
cating liquor (including methylated spiritsand methylated
ether), the registrationof clubs, and the licensingof theatres
and music halls;and forpurposesconnectedtherewith. (Intoxi-
catingLiquor and Licensing.)
22. An Act to provide for the administrationby the Ministry of
Labour ofthe publicserviceinconnectionwith non -contributory
old age pensions, and to amend the law with respectto the
determinationof claims for, and questionsrelatingto, such
pensions. (Old Age Pensions (Administration).)
23. An Act to confirmand give effectto an agreement made between
the Ministryof Commerce and the LisburnElectricSupply
Company , Limited,with respectto the transmissionlineto be
constructedby thesaidCompany forcarryingelectricalenergy
from Belfastto Lisburn. (Lisburn ElectricSupply Company
(Agreement).)

relatingto the establishment ofan Agricultural

purposes connected therewith .

WHEREAS ithas been agreedbetweenthe Commissionersof
His Majesty'sPublic Works and Buildingsof the one part and the
Ministryof Finance of the other part that the lands known as the
Great Park situateat Hillsboroughin theCounty ofDown shallbe
conveyed to the Ministryof Finance and itisintendedthat the con-
veyance to the saidlandsshallbe executedas soon as may be
AND WHEREAS the MinistryofFinanceand the Ministryof
Agriculturearedesirousthatthereshallbe establishedwithinthe said
Great Park an AgriculturalResearch Station(hereinafterreferredto as
" the Station") forthepurposeof carryingout researchinanimal
nutritionand conductingexperimentsand investigationsrelating
to animalsand to crops
AND WHEREAS it has been representedto the Ministry of
Finance that persons representingthe Ministry of Agriculture, the
FacultyofAgricultureoftheQueen'sUniversityof Belfast,theUlster
Farmers' Union and the UlsterAgriculturalOrganizationSociety
(hereinafterreferredtoas "theNominatingBodies")aredesirousof
undertaking the controland management of the Station
AND WHEREAS the Trustees have been selected as such
representativesas aforesaidby the Nominating Bodies as follows:-
The said James Scott Gordon James Pimlott and Josias
Cunningham by the MinistryofAgriculture
The saidGeorgeScottRobertsonand RobertRae by theFaculty
of Agricultureof Queen's University
The said William Robert Morrow Alexander John McDonnell
Pilkingtonand John Martin Mark by the UlsterFarmers '
Union and
The saidHaroldAdrianMilneBarbourby theUlsterAgricultural
OrganizationSociety
AND WHEREAS it is intended that a Bill shall be introduced
into the Parliament of Northern Ireland for the confirmation of this
agreement so soon as the saidintended conveyance shallhave been
executed
NOW THIS INDENTURE WITNESSETH that itishereby
agreed by and between the partieshereto as follows:-
1. (a) The Ministryof Finance shallpermit the Trusteesto use and
occupy allthatpartofthe GreatPark situateat Hillsborough
in the County of Down ,containing485 acres2 roods and
13perchesstatutemeasure,orthereabouts,asshown on the
map heretoannexedand thereuponedgedred,togetherwith
allbuildingsand appurtenances on the said lands, as an
AgriculturalResearch Stationforthe purposeshereinbefore
mentioned .
(b) The MinistryofFinance shallalsopermit the Trusteesto use
and occupy threecottagesat the main entranceto the said
Great Park ,and one cottageknown as the Upper Lodge at
the rearentranceof the saidGreat Park ,the boundariesof

which cottagesarealsoshown on thesaidmap and thesites AD .1927.

(c) The Ministryof Financeshallpermitthe Trusteesto have
accessto the saidlands over the roadways colouredgreen
on the saidmap and to have the rightto reasonableuse of
the road colouredblueon the saidmap .
(d) The Ministryof Finance shallpermit the Trusteesto draw
water from the lake adjoiningthe saidland forthe purpose
of watering cattleor other animals.
Provided that-
(i.) The Ministryof Finance and the Ministryof Agricultureshall
have the rightto use the roads colouredyellowon the said
map forpersonson footor withhorsescartsorothervehicles
and live stock and the said Ministries undertake to make
good any exceptionaldamage caused to thesaidroadsby the
transportthereonoffelledtimber but felledtimbershallnot
be transportedbetween the pointsmarked D. and E. and
pointsmarked F. and G. on the saidmap save with the con-
sentoftheTrusteespreviouslyobtainedinwriting.
(ii.) The Ministryof Finance shallhave the rightto make borings
sinkwellsand carryout suchotheroperationsinthe field
marked A. on the saidmap as itmay deem necessaryforthe
purposes of the water supply to HillsboroughCastle
and no similaroperationsshall be undertaken by the
Trusteesthereonor adjacentthereto.
(iii.) The fieldmarked B. on the saidmap shallbe utilizedby the
Trusteesforgrazingpurposesonly.
(iv.) Plansforalteringthesanitaryarrangementsofexistingbuildings
and plans of the sanitaryarrangements of new buildings
shallbe submittedby the Trusteestothe MinistryofFinance
forapprovaland no suchalterationor new sanitaryarrange-
ment shallbe made withoutsuch approval.
(v.) The Trusteesshallat alltimes prevent theiranimals or any
animalsby them permittedto be on the saidlandsfrom
approachingthe saidlakeand forthe purposeof preventing
the accessof any such animals to the saidlake shallerect
such fencesas may be requiredby the Ministryof Finance.
2. There shallbe paidby theMinistryof Finance to the Trustees
on such dates as may be agreed upon such sums as may be provided
by the Parliament of Northern Ireland not exceeding in the whole
the sum of thirtythousand pounds .
3. The moneys paid to the Trustees under the provisionsof
paragraph two of thesepresentsshallbe used by the Trusteesas a
CapitalFund fortheerectionof new buildingstheinitialreconditioning
of existingbuildingstheiralterationand extensionthe purchase of
equipment and stock and for likepurposes in connexion with the
Station .

as aforesaid .

Fund maintainin good and substantialrepairboth internallyand
externallyallexistingbuildingsand allbuildingsto be erectedand
extended by them and allplantand machinery and keep ingood order
and repairallroadsfencesand erectionson the saidlandsand alsothe
roads colouredgreen on the map hereto annexed and preserve the
amenitiesofthesaidlandsand willnot usethesaidlandsand buildings
forany purposesotherthan thoseof the Station.
7.The Trusteesshallappointand shallpay out of the said
Endowment Fund allsuchstaffasmay be necessarytocarryout the
purposesforwhich the Stationisestablishedand shallprovidesuch
facilitiesastheMinistryofAgriculturemay reasonablyrequireforthe
training of students.
8.The Trusteesshallhave power tocarryoutallsuch transactions
asmay be necessaryor properforthepurposesoftheStationand in
particularto purchaseand sellstockto conduct experimentsforany
publicdepartmentor body orany privatepersonto chargefeesfor
servicesrendered privilegesaffordedand work done and to receive
giftsand bequestsforthepurposesoftheStation.
9. The Trusteesshallkeep such accounts as may be required
by theMinistryofAgricultureand shallmake provisionfortheaudit
of such accountsby an auditoror auditorsto be approved by the
MinistryofFinanceand shallpublishtheiraccountssoauditedannually,
togetherwith an annual reportof theirproceedings.

the landsand thefunds or eitherofthem or any partofeitherof them

12.-(a) Whenever a vacancy shallhappen in the number of the
Trustees a new Trustee shallforthwith be appointed to fillsuch
vacancy .
(b) The mode of appointinga new Trusteehereofin the placeof
an originalTrusteeor any Trusteesucceedingmediatelyor immediately
in hisplaceshallbe vestedin such one of the Nominating Bodies as
nominated the originalTrustee.
(c) Trusteesrepresentingthe Ministryof Agricultureshallif
establishedofficerson the staffof the Ministry of Agriculturehold
officeso longas they continueto be officialsof that Ministryor until
a new Trusteehas been nominated by the Ministryof Agriculturein
their place: Trustees representingthe Faculty of Agricultureof
Queen's Universityshallhold officeso long as they continueto hold
the appointments hereinbeforementioned the other Trusteesshall
hold officefora periodof fiveyears.
(d) A Trustee nominated to filla casual vacancy shallhold
officeonlyso longas theTrustee inwhose placehe isappointedwould
have held office.
(e) If a new Trustee shallnot be appointed within sixmonths
of theoccurrenceofa vacancytheMinistryofFinancemay appoint
a new Trusteeto fillsuch vacancy .
13. These presentsare conditionalon theirconfirmationby an
Act of Parliament of Northern Ireland as herein before recited and the
saidintendedAct may containprovisionsforincorporatingtheTrustees
and forgivingeffecttotheagreementhereincontainedsothatitmay
bind the Trusteesso incorporated.

CHAPTER 2 .
An Act to apply certainSums out of the Consoli-
dated Fund of Northern Ireland to the service
of the years ending on the thirty-firstday of
March ,nineteenhundred and twenty -seven,and
the thirty-firstday of March ,nineteen hundred
and twenty -eight. [31stMarch ,1927.]
BEE itenactedby the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
for the purpose of making good the supply which the
House of Commons have, in pursuance of recommenda-
tionsfrom the Governor of Northern Ireland,granted to
His Majesty in thisSessionof Parliament, as follows:-
1. The Ministryof Finance may issueout of the
Consolidated Fund of Northern Ireland, and apply
towards making good the supply grantedto His Majesty
forthe serviceoftheyear endingon thethirty-firstday
ofMarch ,nineteenhundred and twenty-seven,the sum of
one hundred and fifty-eightthousand,one hundred and
fifty-seven pounds .
2. The Ministryof Finance may issueout of the
said Consolidated Fund , and apply towards making
good thesupplygrantedtoHis Majestyfortheserviceof
the year ending on the thirty-firstday of March ,nineteen
hundred and twenty-eight,the sum of one million,nine
hundred and eighty-one thousand, four hundred and
fiftypounds .

which such Fund is available .

An Act to regulate the sale on commission of
horticulturalproduce .
BE
[31stMay , 1927.]
E itenacted by the King's most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthesame,asfollows:-
1.-(1) Where in the case of any horticultural
produce consigned for saleon commission the salesman
makes a charge by way of commission or otherwise, he
shallenter in a book kept by him for the purpose the
names of the owner or consignor of the produce and
of every purchaser, and the pricepaid or agreed to be
paidby eachpurchaser,and shallas soon as practicable
afterthe sale send by post or deliverto the owneror consignor an account containing the following
particulars:-
(a) the actualpricepaidor agreedto be paid for
the produce,and where thereisany variation
inprice,thenumber,weightor quantitysold,
or agreed to be sold, at each price;and
(b) the commissionor otherchargemade by the
salesmanforsellingtheproduce,togetherwith
detailsof any chargesmade for servicesin
connection with the sale; and
(c) the amounts, ifany, paid or payableby the
salesman on behalfof the owner or consignor
in connection with the sale,with detailsthereof.
(2) Ifon any suchsaleas aforesaidany produceis
bought by the salesman or by any person on hisbehalf,
the fact shall be stated in the account ; but nothing
in this provisionshallbe construed as rendering any
such transaction, if otherwiseillegal, legal.
(3) If any person failsto make any entry,or send
or deliverany account, or sends an account not con-

is falsein any material particular, he shallbe liable
on summary convictionin the caseof a firstoffenceto a

1. The Ministryof Finance may issueout of the
ConsolidatedFund of Northern Ireland, and apply
towardsmaking good thesupplygrantedtoHis Majesty
for the serviceof the year ending on the thirty-firstday
of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-eight,the sum of
fivemillion,ninety-eightthousand and fifty-two pounds .
2.-(1) The Ministryof Finance may borrow from
any person, by the issueof Treasury Billsor otherwise,
on the creditofthe saidsum ,any sum orsums not exceed-
ing in the whole two million, fivehundred thousand
pounds .
(2) The date of payment of any Treasury Bills
issued under this section shall be a date not later than the
thirty-firstday of March ,nineteenhundred and twenty-
eight, and sectionsix of the Treasury BillsAct , 1877
(which relatesto the renewalof bills) shallnot apply
with respectto those Bills.
(3) Any money borrowed otherwise than on
Treasury Billsshallbe repaid, with any interestdue
thereon, out of the growing produce of the said Con-
solidatedFund at any date not laterthan the quarter
next succeeding to that in which the money was
borrowed .
(4) Any money borrowed under this sectionshall
be placed to the creditof the account of the Exchequer
of Northern Ireland, and shallform part of the said
ConsolidatedFund , and be availablein any manner in
which such Fund is available .

SCHEDULE .
1
RESOLUTION .
The Conference, taking note of the difficultiesarisingunder the
law relatingto workmen's compensation in the administrationof
money awarded in one part of the Empire to beneficiariesresident
or becoming residentin anotherpartof the Empire ,isof opinionthat
arrangementsshouldbe made between the differentpartsofthe Empire
whereby any sum awarded to such beneficiariesmay ,at the requestof
the authorityby which the award ismade , be transferredto and
administeredby thecompetentauthorityinthatpartoftheEmpire
inwhich suchbeneficiariesreside. Itaccordinglyinvitestheseveral
Governments of the Empire to take such stepsby way of legislation
orotherwiseaseachmay considernecessaryand appropriateforthe
purpose of promoting such arrangements.
CHAPTER 14 .

respects Northern Ireland .
[21st December ,1927.]
WHEREAS theActs(whetherpassedbytheParlia-of the United Kingdom or by the
Parliament of Northern Ireland) mentioned in the
Scheduleto thisAct are,in so faras they are in forcein
Northern Irelandand are temporary in theirduration,
limitedto expire on the thirty-firstday of December ,
nineteenhundred and twenty -seven :
And whereas itisexpedientto provideforthe continuance
as in thisAct mentioned of those Acts , and of the enact-
ments amending or affectingthe same :
Be it thereforeenacted by the King's most Excellent
Majesty, and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-

CHAPTER 16 .
An Act toconsolidate,as respectsNorthern Ireland,
the law relating to compensation to workmen
for injuries suffered in the course of their
employment . [21st December , 1927.]
W HEREAS itisexpedientto consolidate, as respects
Northern Ireland, the law relatingto compensa-
tion to workmen for injuriessufferedin the course of
theiremployment :
And whereas certainprovisions(inthisAct referred
to as "the reservedprovisions")contained in the enact-
ments relatingto such compensation enacted by the
Parliament of the United Kingdom relateto matters in
respect of which the Parliament of Northern Ireland
have not power to make laws :
And whereas it is expedient for convenience of
referencethat certainof the reservedprovisions,namely
thosewhich relateto appealsto the Court ofAppeal and
House of Lords ,and to the investment of certainsums in
the Post OfficeSavings Bank , should be set out in the
Fourth Scheduleto thisAct in the manner in which they
are applicableto matters arisingunder the provisionsof
thisAct ,and that such of the reservedprovisionsas are
contained in the Workmen's Compensation Act , 1925,
passedby the Parliamentofthe United Kingdom ,should
be set out in the Fifth Schedule to this Act :
Be it therefore enacted by the King's most
Excellent Majesty, and the Senate and the House of
Commons ofNorthernIrelandinthispresentParliament
assembled,and by theauthorityofthesame,asfollows:-
PART I.
COMPENSATION FOR INJURIES .
Right to Compensation .
1.- (1) If in any employment personalinjury by
accidentarisingout of and in the course of the employ-
ment iscaused to a workman ,hisemployer shall,subject
as hereinaftermentioned,be liableto pay compensation
in accordance with the provisionshereinaftercontained:
Provided that-
(a) The employer shallnot be liableunder thisAct
in respect of any injury which does not
disable the workman for a period of at least

## Page 59

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] Workmen's CompensationAct [Ch .16.] 53
(NorthernIreland),1927.
three days from earningfullwages at the
work at which he was employed ;
(b) Ifitisproved that the injuryto a workman is
attributable to the serious and wilful mis-
conduct of that workman , any compensation
claimedin respectofthatinjuryshall,unless
the injury resultsin death or seriousand
permanent disablement, be disallowed.
(2) For thepurposesofthisAct,an accidentresult-
ingin the death or seriousand permanent disablementof
a workman shall be deemed to arise out of and in the
course of his employment , notwithstanding that the
workman was at the time when the accidenthappened
actingin contraventionof any statutoryor otherregula-
tionapplicableto hisemployment ,or of any ordersgiven
by or on behalf of his employer, or that he was acting
without instructionsfrom his employer, ifsuch act was
done by the workman forthe purposesof and in connec-
tionwith his employer'strade or business.
(3) This Act shallapply notwithstandingany con-
tract to the contrary, whether made before or after
the commencement of thisAct ,except that where under
thisAct the provisionsof a scheme are substitutedfor
the provisionsof thisAct , the employer shallbe liable
only in accordance with the scheme .
2.-(1) The compensation shallbe payable to or
for the benefitof the workman , or, where death results
from the injury,to or forthe benefitof his dependants
as providedby thisAct.
(2) Where therearebothtotaland partialdepend-
antsnothing inthisAct shallbe construedas preventing
the compensation being allottedpartlyto the totaland
partlyto the partialdependants.

threehundred pounds ;

duringthesaidthreeyearsshall,forthepurposes

10.For the purposes of the provisionsof thisAct
relatingto " earnings" and " averageweeklyearnings"
of a workman ,the followingrulesshallbe observed :-
(i) Average weekly earningsshallbe computed in
such manner as isbest calculatedto give the
rateper week at which the workman was being
remunerated : Provided that where by reason
of the shortnessof the time during which the
workman has been in the employment of his
employer,or the casualnature of the employ-
ment , or the terms of the employment , it is
impracticableat the date of the accidentto
compute the rateof remuneration,regardmay
be had to the average weekly amount which ,
during the twelve months previous to the
accident,was beingearnedby a personinthe
same grade employed at the same work by the
same employer, or, if there is no person so
employed , by a person in the same grade
employedinthesame classofemployment and
in the same district;
(ii) Where the workman had enteredinto con-
current contracts of service with two or more
employersunder which he worked at one time
forone such employer and at anothertime for
another such employer, his average weekly
earningsshallbe computed as ifhis earnings
under allsuch contractswere earningsin the
employment of the employer forwhom he was
working at the time ofthe accident;
(iii) Employment by the same employershallbe
taken to mean employment by the same em-
ployer in the grade in which the workman was
employed at the time of the accident, un

Conditionsof Compensation.
14.- (1) Proceedingsfor the recovery under this
Act of compensation for an injury shallnot be main-
tainableunlessnoticeof the accidenthas been given as
soon as practicableafter the happening thereof and
beforethe workman has voluntarilyleftthe employment
in which he was injured, and unlessthe claim for com-
pensationwith respectto such accidenthas been made
within six months from the occurrence of the accident
causingthe injury,or,incaseofdeath,withinsixmonths
from the time of death :

(a) the want of or any defect or inaccuracy in
such notice shall not be a bar to the mainten-

(NorthernIreland),1927.
ance of such proceedingsif the employer is
provedtohave had knowledgeoftheaccident
from any other source at or about the time

employer isnot, or would not, ifa noticeor
an amended noticewere then given and the
hearingpostponed,be prejudicedinhisdefence
by the want , defect or inaccuracy, or that
such want , defect or inaccuracy was occa-
sioned by mistake, absence from Northern

(b) the failureto make a claim withinthe period

(2) Noticeinrespectof any injuryunder thisAct
may be given eitherin writing or orallyto the em-

Application to specialClasses of Persons .
33.-(1) This Act shallnot apply to persons in
the naval or militaryor air serviceof the Crown , but
otherwiseshallapply to workmen employed by or under

at the commencement ofthisAct ,but any such scheme ,
order, rule, regulation, agreement, or award , or other
instrument, or other thing, shallcontinue in forceand
have effectas if certified, issued, made or done under
this Act .
(3) The repealof sub-section(2) of sectionsixteen
of the Workmen's Compensation Act , 1906, shallnot
affectthe applicationof the Workmen's Compensation
Acts, 1897 to 1900, to casesto which by virtueof that
sub-sectionthey are to continue to apply.
52. This Act may be cited as the Workmen's
Compensation Act (Northern Ireland),1927.
Section 21 .
SCHEDULES .
FIRST SCHEDULE .
ARBITRATION , & C.
1. For the purpose of settlingany matter which under this
Act isto be settledby arbitration,ifany committee,representative
ofan employerand hisworkmen ,existswithpower tosettlematters
under thisAct in the case of the employer and workmen ,the matter
shall,unlesseitherparty objectsby noticein writingsentto the other
party beforethe committee meet to considerthe matter, be settled
by the arbitrationof such committee,or be referredby them in their
discretionto arbitrationas hereinafterprovided.
2.If eitherparty so objects, or there is no such committee,
or the committee so refers the matter or fails to settle the matter
within six months from the date of the claim, the matter shallbe

## Page 101

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] Workmen's CompensationAct [Ch .16.] 95
(Northern Ireland), 1927 .
settledby a singlearbitratoragreedon by theparties,orintheabsence
of agreement by the judge of the county court, according to the
procedureprescribedby rulesofcourt.
3.-(i) A committee or an arbitratormay ,ifthey orhe thinkfit,
submit any questionof law forthe decisionof the judge ofthe county
court ; and the judge of the county court shall,for the purpose of
proceedingsunder thisAct, have the same powers of procuringthe
attendance of witnessesand the production of documents as ifthe
proceedingswere an actionin the county court.
(ii) The decisionofthejudgeofthe county courton any question
oflaw eitheron a submissionundersub-division(i)ofthisparagraph,
or in any case where he himselfsettlesthe matter under thisAct or
where he givesany decisionor makes any orderunder thisAct ,shall
be final,unlesseitherparty appealstherefromunder and inaccordance
with the reservedprovisionssetout in paragraph 1 of the Fourth
Schedule to this Act .
4. The judgeofthecounty courtmay inany case,ifhe thinksfit,
and shall,ifany party in accordance with rulesof court so requires
and gives securityfor the payment of the prescribedfee, summon
a medical referee to sit with him as assessor .
Ifa medicalrefereeisso summoned on theapplicationofany
party,thatpartyshall,subjecttoany directionsasto costs,be liable
to pay in respectof the attendanceof the medicalrefereesuch feeas
may be prescribedby theMinistryofLabour.
5. Rules of courtmay make provision--
(a) fortheappearanceinany arbitrationunderthisAct ofany
party by some other person;and
(b) for conferringon the judge or clerkofthe crown and peace
in proceedingsunder thisAct powers of making ordersfor
the examinationof witnessesand persons,and fordiscovery,
interrogatories,inspectionofdocuments,and furtherpar-
ticulars, and of granting a new trial.
6.- (i) The costs of and incidentalto the arbitrationand
proceedingsconnectedtherewithshallbe in the discretionof the
committee,arbitrator,orjudgeofthecountycourt,subjectasrespects
such judge to rulesof court.
(ii) The costs, whether before a committee or an arbitrator
or inthe county court,shallnot exceedthe limitprescribedby rulesof
court,and shallbe taxed inmanner prescribedby thoserulesand such
taxationmay be reviewedby thejudgeofthecountycourt.
7. Where a reference is made to a medical refereeunder section
sixteenor sectionnineteenof thisAct ,or where on an applicationfor
the registrationof a memorandum of agreement a reportof a medical
refereeisrequiredunder thisAct to be obtained,thereshall,subject
toany directionsasto costsand totheprovisionshereinaftercontained,
be payableby theapplicantforthereferenceorfortheregistrationof
the memorandum such feeinrespectofthe remunerationand expenses
of the medicalrefereeas the Ministryof Labour may prescribe,and
provisionmay be made by rulesofcourtforthepayment ofsuchfees
throughtheclerkofthecrownand peace.

CHAPTER 17 .
An Act to provide for the granting of licencesfor
the sale of milk under specialdesignations.
BE
[21stDecember, 1927.]
E itenactedby the King'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authority of the same , as follows:-
1.-(1) A person shallnot,eitherby himselfor by
underspecialany servantor agent,exceptunderand in accordance
designations. with a licencegranted by the MinistryofHome Affairs

## Page 109

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] Sale of Milk Act 103[Ch .17.]
(Northern Ireland), 1927.
(a) sellor offeror expose for sale any milk as
" certified," " Grade A ," " tuberculintested"
or "T. T.," or under such other designation
as may be from time to time prescribedby
regulationsmade under thisAct ; or
(b) on or in connectionwith any saleor offerfor
sale or proposed sale of any milk or in any
advertisement, circularor notice relatingto
any milk, describeor referto the same as
" certified," " Grade A.," "tuberculintested"
or " T. T.," or by any other designation
prescribedas aforesaid,or use any description
or designation including or resembling any
such descriptionor designation.
(2) A licencemay be granted for the purposes of
this sectionfor such period, and subjectto such terms
and conditions(includingconditionsas to the payment
of fees),as may be prescribedby regulationsmade under
thisAct ; and a licenceso granted may be at any time
suspended or revoked by the Ministryof Home Affairs
by reason of the non -compliance of the holder thereof
with any conditionsprescribedas aforesaid, or for any
other reason which the said Ministry may deem to be
sufficient .
(3) If any person is guilty of a contraventionof
the foregoingprovisionsof thissectionhe shallbe liable,
on summary conviction, for the firstoffence, to a fine
not exceedingten pounds, and for the secondor any
subsequent offence to a fine not exceeding twenty
pounds , and ,ifthe offenceis a continuingoffence, to a
further fine not exceeding two pounds for each day
during which the offencecontinues:
Provided that,where a person not having a licence
granted by the Ministryof Home Affairsunder thisAct
isconvictedof sellingmilk or exposing or offeringmilk
forsalein contraventionof the foregoingprovisionsof
thissection,he shallbe liable,for the firstoffence,to a
fineof not lessthan two pounds ,and for the second or
any subsequent offence,to a fineof not lessthan five
pounds .
(4) Any authorised officershall have power to
take and submit for analysisor for bacteriologicalor
other examination samples of any milk offered or

B
[21stDecember,1927.]

CHAPTER 19 .
An Act to consolidate, with amendments , the
enactments relatingto quarries,and forpurposes
connected therewith . [21stDecember ,1927.]
BEE itenactedby theKing'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same .as follows:-
PART I.
PROVISIONS AS TO SAFETY AND EMPLOYMENT .
1. For the prevention of dangerous accidents,
and forensuringthe safetyofpersonsemployed ,in every
quarry, the followingprovisionsshallhave effect:-
(a) The working ofthe sidesand ofthe overburden
of the quarry shall be carriedon so as to
prevent dangerous fallsof material;
Genera
provisions as
to safety .
H

## Page 114

108 Quarries Act [17 & 18 GEO .5.][Ch .19.]
A.D. 1927 .
General
(NorthernIreland),1927.
(b) The topofthequarry,and any openingorshaft
made for the purpose of quarryingshall,if
dangerous,be kept securelyfenced;
(c) If quarryingwork is carriedon afterdark.
the quarry shallbe under the supervisionof
a competent person appointed by the owner,
occupieroragentforthe purposeof such work ;
(d) Effectivemeasures shallbe taken for securing
and maintainingsufficientand suitablelighting
in every part of the quarry in which persons
are working ;
(e) No explosivesshallbe taken intoorused inany
quarry except explosivesprovided by the
owner, occupieror agent ;
(f) Due and effectivewarning shall be given
beforeblastingis commenced and when it is
finished .
2. The followingprovisionsshallhave effectin
tomachineryconnectionwiththeuseofmachineryina quarry:-
provisionsas
(a) A personshallnot cleanany partof a prime
mover or any transmissionmachinery whilein
motion,or any part of a machine ,the cleaning
of which would expose that personto riskof
injury eitherfrom that machine or from any
adjacentmachinery ;
(b) Every craneshallbe providedwith an efficient
catch or an efficientbrake ;
(c) Every crane or winch shall have the safe
workingloadplainlymarked upon it,and no
crane or winch shall be used for any load
exceeding the safeworking load ;
(d) Every moving part of the prime mover and all
dangerous parts of the machinery, including
transmissionmachinery, whether in an engine
house or not,shalleitherbe so fenced or be in
such positionor of such constructionas to be
safe to every person employed or working at
the quarry ;
(e) A belt, strap or rope, when not in use, shall
not be allowedto restor rideupon a revolving
shaft which forms part of the transmission
machinery .

3.-(1) Every steam boiler, whether separateor
one of a range,in use at a quarry-
(a) shallhave attachedto it-
(i) a suitablesafetyvalve,separatefrom any
stop-valve, which shallbe so adjustedas
topermit the steam to escapeat a working
pressurenot greaterthan the maximum
permissibleworkingpressureand shall,in
the case of any new boilertaken intouse
afterthe commencement of thisAct , be
fixeddirectlyto the boiler; and
(ii) a correctsteam pressuregauge connected
to the steam spaceand easilyvisibleby
the boilerattendant, which shallindicate
the pressure of steam in the boilerin
pounds per squareinch,and have marked
upon itin a distinctivecolourthemaximum
permissibleworking pressure;and
(iii) at leastone water gauge of transparent
material to show the water level in the
boiler,and,ifthe working pressurein the
boilernormallyexceedsfortypounds per
square inch, the gauge shallbe provided
with an efficientguard, but not so as to
obstructthe readingofthe gauge ;and
(iv) a suitablestopvalveconnectingtheboiler
to the steam pipe ; and
(v) where itis one of two or more boilers,

easilyvisible; and
(b) shallbe providedwith means forattachinga
test pressure gauge ; and
(c) unless externallyfiredor of the water tube
type,shallbe provided with a suitablefusible
plug or an efficientlow-water alarm device.
For the purposes of thissub-sectiona lever-valve
shallnot be deemed a suitablesafetyvalve unlessthe
weight issecuredon the leverin the correctposition.
(2) Every steam boilerand allits fittingsand
attachments shall be maintained in efficientworking
order .

examined by a competent person at leastonce in every

4.- (1) If,on complaint by an inspector,a courtof
summary jurisdictionissatisfiedeither-
(a) thatany partofthe machineryor plantused
in a quarry is in such a conditionor is so
constructedor isso placed that itcannot be
used withoutdanger ofbodilyinjury;or

anythingisdone inany quarryinsuch a manner
as to threatenor tend to the bodilyinjuryof
any person ;
the courtmay ,as the casemay require,by order-
(i) prohibitthe use of that part of the machinery
or plant,or,ifitiscapable of repairor altera-
tion, prohibititsuse untilit isduly repaired
or altered ; or
(ii) requirethe occupierto take such stepsas may
be specifiedin the order for remedying the
danger complained of.
(2) Where a complaint has been made under this
section, the court, or a justice may , on application
ex parte by the inspectorto the effectthat the use
of any such part of the machinery or plant involves
imminent danger to life, make an interim order pro-
hibiting, eitherabsolutelyor subjectto conditions, the
use thereofuntilthe earliestopportunityforhearingand
determining the complaint.
(3) In the event of any contraventionof an order
made under thissection, the occupier, and , in the case
of a contraventionrespectingany part of the machinery
or plant, any person entitledto controlthe use of that
part,shallbe guiltyof an offenceand liableto a finenot
exceeding twenty pounds, and to a further fine not
exceedingfivepounds foreach day on which the contra-
vention continues after conviction thereof .

PART V.
SUPPLEMENTARY .
29.- (1) This Act shallapply to every place (not
beinga mine)in whichpersonswork ingettingstone,
slate,sand,clayor otherminerals;and every such place
isin thisAct referredto as a quarry .
(2) For the purposesof thisAct a quarryshallbe
deemed to comprise-
(a) any premisesin or adjacentto, and belonging
to,a quarry in which the only processcarried
on is a process ancillaryto the getting of
theminerals,includingthe breaking,crushing,
grinding, screening, washing and dressing of
such minerals ; and
(b) any lineor siding(not being part of a railway
within the meaning of the Railway Employ-
ment (Prevention of Accidents) Act, 1900)
used exclusivelyinconnectionwith,and forthe
purposesof,a quarry ;and
(c) any dock , wharf, quay , or landing stage
adjacentto and belongingto a quarry and used
exclusivelyfor purposes connected therewith.
(3) Ifany questionarises(otherwisethan in legal
proceedings)whether a quarry isa quarry to which this
Act applies, or whether any place or premises isor are
comprised within any such quarry, such questionshall
be referredto the Ministryof Commerce ,whose decision
thereon shall be final.

(NorthernIreland),1927.
FIRST SCHEDULE .
RULES FOR GENERAL APPLICATION .
PreventionofDangerous Accidentsin a Quarry.
1. The owner , occupier, or agent shallsee that a sufficient
supplyofpropermaterialsand appliancesforthepurposeof carrying
out the provisionsof the Act and these rulesand any regulations
made inpursuanceoftheserules,and forthepurposeof ensuringthe
safetyofthequarryand thepersonsemployed,isalwaysprovided.
2. Every personemployed at the quarry shallcomply with the
provisionsof theserules,and of any regulationsmade by the owner ,
occupieror agent in pursuance of theserules,and with such direc-
tionsconcerningsafetyand disciplineas may be givento him by
personsinauthorityover him .
3. Every workman employed at the quarryshall,beforecom
mencingwork,and duringthecourseofit,and especiallyafterblast-
ing,make a carefulexaminationofhisworking place,and remove any
looserock,stonesorgroundwhichmightbe dangerous.
Safety of Persons Employed .
4. Secure means of access, by which allpersonsemployed can
go to and from theirworking places, shallbe provided and main-
tainedingood conditionby the owner,occupier,or agent.
5.Every personemployed at the quarryshall, beforecom-
mencingwork,satisfyhimselfas to the safetyof the rope or other
applianceprovidedforhisuse,and shallnot useanythingwhichhe
finds unsafe .
Regulationof Supply, Use and Storageof Explosives.
6. In quarrieswhere blastingis done dailyit shall,as far as
possible,be done at fixedstatedintervals.
7. The owner,occupier, or agent shallmake regulationsas to
intervalsand signalsforblasting,copiesof which shallbe kept con-
stantlyaffixedin the officeat the quarry and in a sufficientnumber
of placesin and adjacentto the quarry.
8. A sufficientnumber of proper sheltersshallbe provided by
the owner,occupier,or agent,and used by the personsemployed,
unlessallpersonsemployedleavethequarryduringblasting,and retire
to a safe distance .
9. The owner , occupier or agent of any quarry in which
explosivesare used shallprovide a suitableplace or magazine for
storageof any explosivekept at the quarry.
10. Detonators shallbe kept in secure and securelylocked
boxesseparatefrom any otherexplosive,and suchboxesshallnot be
placedinany receptaclecontainingotherexplosives.
11.Every workman or gang of workmen temporarilyin pos-
sessionofexplosivesshallkeepthem,when notrequiredforimmediate
use,ina properlyconstructedlockedplaceorchestprovidedexclusively
&

## Page 133

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] 127Quarries Act [Ch .19.]
(NorthernIreland),1927.
forthepurpose; and such placeshallnot be within,and suchchest A.D.1927.
shallnot be takeninto,any placewherethereisa fire,or any mess-room or work -room or similarplacewhere personscongregate. The
interiorof every such lockedplaceand chestshallbe kept cleanand
freefrom grit.
12. No person shallsmoke , or have any naked light, whilst
carrying,handlingor usingexplosive,or whilstwithintwenty feet
of any personwho isso doing ; but thisruleshallnot preventthe use
of a naked lightforfiringa shot.
13. Where explosivescontainingnitro-glycerineand likelyto
be affectedby coldor frostare used or kept foruse,proper warming
pans shallbe provided by the owner or occupier, and allsuch ex-
plosivesshall, immediately beforeuse, be softenedin such warming
pans ifthey show any signsof hardness.
14. No explosiveshallbe rammed with violence or forcibly
pressedintoa hole. If two or more cartridgesare used in a drilled
hole,theyshallnotbe tiedor bunchedtogether.
15. No tool,otherthan a rammer composed only of wood ,shall
be used forpushing any explosiveintoa hole.
16. No toolofironorsteel,or partlyofironorsteel,shallbe used
forstemming any hole.
17. No boring shallbe done in,or metal toolintroducedinto,
any holeorsocketofa holewhichhas beenblastedwithgeligniteor
any nitro-glycerineexplosive.
18. Ifa shot missesfire,or does not explode atthetime when it
was intendedto explode,no person shallgo or be allowedtogo nearit
untilithas exploded,or untilan intervalhas elapsedof not lessthan
one hour in the caseof firingby fuse,or ten minutes in the case of
firingby electricity. The personwhose shothas apparentlymissed fire
shailimmediately give warning of the occurrence to allpersons
likelyto be affected, and to the person under whose directionhe
works .
19. A charge which has missed fireshallnot be unrammed ,
bored or picked out; but this requirement shallnot precludethe
extractionof the detonatorby means of any apparatus approved by
the MinistryofCommerce forenablinga detonatorto be removed with
safetyafterthe shot-holehas been charged.
20. Ifitisnecessaryto borea holeneara chargewhich has missed
fire,careshallbe takentoboretheholeinsucha manner asnotto affect
or ignitethe unexploded charge.
21. After a second shot has been firednear a missed-fireshot,
carefulsearchshallbe made by a competent personforthe unexploded
charge .
Regulationof Use of Machinery and Plant.
22.Linesof railsand pointsshallbe kept in efficientorder,
having regardto the natureof the traffic.

9.-(1) ThisAct may be citedastheTrade Disputes
and Trade Unions Act (Northern Ireland), 1927, and interpreta-
shall be construed as one with the Trade Union Acts ,
1871 to 1917 , and this Act and the Trade Union Acts ,
1871 to 1917,may be citedtogetheras the Trade Union
Acts (Northern Ireland), 1871 to 1927.
(2) For the purposesof thisAct--
(a) the expression" strike" means the cessation
of work by a body of persons employed in
any tradeor industryactingincombination,
or a concerted refusal, or a refusalunder a
common understandingof any number of
personswho are,or have been so employed ,
tocontinuetowork ortoacceptemployment ;
(b) the expression" lock-out " means the closing
of a place of employment or the suspension
of work , or the refusalby an employer to
continuetoemployany number ofpersons
employed by him inconsequenceofa dispute,
done with a view tocompellingthosepersons,
or to aid another employer in compelling
personsemployed by him ,to acceptterms or
conditionsof or affectingemployment ; and
(c) a strikeor lock-out shallnot be deemed to
be calculated to coerce the Government
unlesssuch coercionought reasonablyto be
expected as a consequence thereof.
(3) References in this Act to enactments of the
Parliament of the United Kingdom shall, unless the
context otherwiserequires, be construed as references
to thoseenactments as they apply inNorthern Ireland.
(4) The enactments mentioned in the Second
Schedule to thisAct are hereby repealedto the extent
specifiedin the thirdcolumn of that Schedule.

(1)ofthissection,shallbe deemed a disorderlyhouse,and
the personoccupying orratedasoccupierofthesame shall
be liabletoa penaltynotexceedingfivepoundsforevery
day on which such premises are so used as a theatreor
music hall .
(3) A theatreor music hallshallnot be deemed tobe
a place of public entertainment within the meaning of
sectionfifty-one of the Public Health Acts Amendment
Act , 1890 .

CHAPTER 23 .
An Act to confirm and give effectto an agreement
made between the Ministry of Commerce and
the Lisburn ElectricSupply Company , Limited,
with respect to the transmission line to be
constructedby the said Company forcarrying
electricalenergy from Belfastto Lisburn.
[21stDecember ,1927.]
WHERHEREAS by an agreement,datedthetwelfthday
of October, nineteenhundred and twenty -seven,
made between the Ministryof Commerce of the one part
and the Lisburn ElectricSupply Company , Limited,
being the undertakersfor the purposes of the Lisburn
ElectricitySpecialOrder,1927 (inthisAct referredto as

## Page 179

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] Lisburn ElectricSupply 173[Ch .23.]
Company (Agreement) Act
(NorthernIreland),1927.
"the Company ") of theotherpart,which agreement is A.D.1927.
set forth in the Schedule to this Act and is in this Act
referredto as " the scheduledagreement," itwas agreed,
upon the conditionsthereinmentioned,that the Ministry
of Commerce should advance a sum of one thousand
fourhundred and fiftypounds totheCompany ,and that
in consideration of the said advance the transmission
lineof the Company from Belfastto Lisburnshouldbe
constructed and maintained by the Company as set
forthin the scheduled agreement,and that the Ministry
ofCommerce should,withrespecttothesaidtransmission
line,have therightssetforthinthescheduledagreement:
And whereas the provisions of the scheduled
agreement cannot take effectwithout the authorityof
Parliament :
Be it, therefore, enacted by the King's most
ExcellentMajesty, and the Senate and the House of
Commons of Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament
assembled,and by theauthorityofthesame,asfollows:-
1.The scheduledagreement ishereby confirmed Confirmation
and shall have effect as if enacted in this Act .
For thepurposesofparagraph11.ofthescheduled
agreement,the passingofthisAct shallbe deemed to be
the approval of each House of the Parliament of
Northern Ireland .
2.----(1) The sum of one thousand fourhundred and
fiftypounds tobe advancedby theMinistryofCommerce
under the scheduledagreementshallbe chargedon and
issuedoutoftheConsolidatedFund ofNorthernIreland,
or the growing produce thereof.
(2) Allsums tobe paidtotheMinistryofCommerce
under thescheduledagreementby way of repayment of
the principalof, and intereston, the sum advanced as
aforesaidshallbe paid into the Exchequer of Northern
Ireland .

3. This Act may be citedas the LisburnElectricShorttitle

SCHEDULE .
AN AGREEMENT made the Twelfth day of October One
Thousand Nine Hundred and Twenty-Seven between the Ministry
ofCommerce forNorthernIreland(hereinaftercalled" theMinistry")
of the one partand the LisburnElectricSupplyCompany Limited
havingtheirregisteredofficeat Coates'BuildingsintheCountyofthe
CityofBelfast(hereinaftercalled" theCompany ")oftheotherpart
whereby it is agreedas follows:-
1. In consideration of the sum of One Thousand Four Hundred
and FiftyPounds advancedby theMinistrytheCompany undertakes
to erect,use and maintain in the constructionof itstransmissionlinefrom Belfastto Lisburn (hereinafterreferredto as " the transmission
line") Messrs. Henley'sPatent Anchor "A " type wooden poles,
fortyfeet long over allwith long cross arms and suspensiontype
insulatorssuitablefor conductors carrying electricalenergy at a
pressureof 33,000voltsand to lay and maintaincablessimilarly
suitableforoperatingat33,000voltsundergroundintheroadscrossed
by thetransmissionlineassetoutintheSpecialOrdergrantedtothe
Company by theElectricityCommissioners.
2.The £1,450providedby theMinistryofCommerce,asaforesaid,
shallbe securedby a Debenture issuedby the Company to the Ministry.
3.No interestshallbe payableon the Debentureuntilsuch
timeas the maximum loaddeliveredto the Company at the Belfast
Terminus of the transmissionlineshallexceed 1,000kilowatts(com-
puted as hereinafterprovided) duringa periodor periodstotalling
one hour in any one day of twenty-four hours or in the alternative
untilpower istransmittedby the Company at a pressurenominally
in excess of 6,600 volts.
4. If and when the Company transmitselectricalenergy over
thetransmissionlineor any partthereofin excessof 1,000K.W. or
ata pressureexceeding6,600volts,asaforesaid,interestshallthereafter
bepaidupon theDebentureattherateof54 percent.perannum ,and
inadditionthecapitalamount oftheadvancemade by the Ministry
on the securityof the Debenture shallbe paid off(a)in full,or (6)by
instalmentsinsuchsums asmay be agreedupon betweentheMinistry
and the Company .
5. The Ministryshallhave the rightfor itselfor itsnominee
ornominees atany time tosetup transformingstationsand totransmit
electricalenergy over the transmissionlineand to make such arrange-
ments with respectto the purchaseand saleof such energy as may be
in excessof the Company's requirementsfor the time being as the
Ministrymay decide: ProvidedhoweverthattheCompany shallhave
the firstclaimupon thecarryingcapacityofthetransmissionlineup
to 1,000kilowattsat 6,600 voltsas aforesaid.

## Page 181

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] [LisburnElectricSupply 175[Ch . 23.]
Company (Agreement)Act
(NorthernIreland),1927.
6. The Ministryor itsnominee shallhave the righton giving A.D.1927.
sixmonths noticeinwritingoftheirintentiontodo soto acquireby
purchasethe propertyinsuch partofthetransmissionlineas isoutside
theLisburnUrban Districtand allsuchlands,rightsand easements,
buildings,works,materialand plantbelongingtotheCompany suitable
toand usedby them forthepurposesofsuchpartofthetransmission
lineasaforesaid,upon thetermsofpayingthethenvalueofsuchpart
of the transmissionlineand allsuch lands, rightsand easements,
buildings,works,materialand plantasaforesaid,suchvalueto be in
case of differencedeterminedby arbitration: Providedthat the
valueof such part of the transmissionlineand such lands,rightsand
easements,buildings, works,materialand plantshallbe deemed to
be theirfairmarket valueat the time of the purchase,due regard
being had to the nature and then conditionof the transmissionline
or suchbuildings,works,materialand plant,and thestateofrepair
thereof,and to the circumstancethatthey arein such a positionas to
be readyforimmediateworking,and tothesuitabilityofthesame for
thepurposesoftheundertakingoftheCompany,and to any loss
occasionedto the Company by severance;but withoutany addition
in respectof compulsorypurchaseor of good willor of any profits
whichmay ormighthave beenor be made from thetransmissionline
orany similarconsiderations: ProvidedalsothattheCompany shall
have the firstclaimupon the carryingcapacityof the transmission
lineup to 1,000kilowattsat 6,600 voltsas aforesaidor alternatively
such otherpressureas may be mutually agreedbetween the Ministry
and the Company .
7. The 1,000 kilowattsaforesaidshallbe computed as being
deliveredto the transmissionlineat the BelfastTerminus at a power
factorof not lessthan .8or at such otherpower factoras willresultin
a reductionin pressureat Lisburn not exceeding10 per cent.
8. The Company shallnot sellor createany mortgage,charge
or burden upon the transmissionline without the consent of the
Ministryof Commerce .
9. The Company shailuntilthe Ministryexercisestherightof
purchaseconferredon itby paragraph6.hereofmaintainthe trans-
missionlineina properstateofrepairand make goodanylossordamage
causedby ordinarywear and tear,over-pressure,accident, flooding,
stormor any othercausewhatsoever.
10.The expression" theCompany " shallincludethe Company ,
itssuccessorsand assigns.
11.This agreementshallnot become effectiveuntilapproved
by eachHouse oftheParliamentofNorthernIreland.

LOCAL ACTS
17, 17 & 18 GEORGE 5.
CHAPTER I.
An Act to simplifythe Collectionand Recovery of
Rates in the Town of Portadown , and for
other purposes . [31stMay ,1927.]
WHEREAS the Town of Portadown is an Urban
District, subjectto the Acts relatingto such districts
in Northern Ireland, and the Urban DistrictCouncil of
Portadown (in thisAct called" the Council" ) are the
urban sanitaryauthorityforthe saiddistrict.
And whereas the expenses of the Council, whether
as an urban districtor sanitaryauthority, are payable
out of the Town rate :
And whereas it is expedient that the Poor Rate
and Town rate should be recoverabletogether:
And whereas itisexpedientthat the owner ,instead
of the occupier, should be liablefor and rated to the
Poor rateand Town ratein respectofthe hereditaments
specifiedin thisAct :
And whereas it is expedient that the other pro-
visions in this Act contained should be enacted :
And whereas the objects aforesaid cannot be
attained without the authority of Parliament :
And whereas in relationto the promotion of the
BillforthisAct the requirementsof the Borough Funds
(Ireland) Act , 1888, have been observed.
MAY IT THEREFORE PLEASE YOUR MAJESTY
That itmay BE ENACTED AND BE IT ENACTED by
the KING'S MOST EXCELLENT MAJESTY by and
with the advice and consent of the Senate and the House
of Commons of Northern Ireland in this present
Parliamentassembled and by the authorityof same
as follows(that isto say):
A.D. 1927 .

1. This Act may be citedas The Portadown Urban

3. In thisAct unlessotherwiseexpresslyprovided
or the context otherwise requires-
" The District " means the Urban District of
Portadown in the County of Armagh as
constitutedfor the time being;
" The Council " means the Urban District Council
of the District;
" Owner " in relation to a hereditament means a
person for the time being receivingfrom the
occupierthe rent payable in respectthereof
whether on his own account or as agent or
trusteefor any other person,or who would so
receive the same if such hereditaments were
let at a rent ;
" The Town Rate " means the generalconsolidated
town rate raised by the Council under the
powers of the Towns Improvement (Ireland)
Act , 1854, and the Public Health (Ireland)
Act ,1878,as extended by any otherActs,the
Water Rate raisedby the Council under the
powers of the PublicHealth (Ireland) Act,
1878, as extended by any other Act, and the
rateraisedby the Councilunder the powers of
the Public Libraries (Ireland) Acts, 1855
to 1920 .
PART II .- RECOVERY OF RATES .
4. The Poor rate and the Town rate may be
demanded together in one demand note and shallbe
recoverablein one sum and allthe enactments relating
tothe apportionment and recoveryofthePoor ratewhich
are in force at the commencement of this Act shall,

6.-(1) The owner insteadof the occupiershallbe

accordingly.
(2) The Councilshallallowtoeachowner who pays
the said rates in pursuance of this sectionwithin one
month afterserviceof the noticedemanding payment of
said ratesa deduction equal to fiveper centum of the
amount so paid .
(3) Whenever the name of any owner liableto be
ratedunder the provisionsof thissectionisunknown ,it
shall be sufficientto rate such owner in the rate book of
the Councilasthe owner ofthe propertyto be ratedby
the descriptionof owner without statinghis name , and
any notice,demand note or other document requiredor
authorised to be sent or served concerning the rates
payableinrespectofthesaidpropertymay be addressed
to " the owner " of the premises(naming the premises)
without furthername or description, and if afterdue
enquirieshave been made the name and addressof such
owner cannot be discoveredmay be sent or served by
deliveringitto some person on the premises.
(4) (a) When any owner israted in pursuance of
the provisionsofsub-section(1) of thissectionin respect
of any hereditaments in the occupation of any tenant
under any contractof tenancy made priorto the passing
of thisAct ,such tenantshallrepay to the owner allsums
paidby the owner duringthecontinuanceofsuch contract
of tenancy on account of the Poor rate and Town rate,
which would but for thisAct have been payable by the
tenant under such contractof tenancy.

(b) Where any owner isratedin pursuanceof the

from the tenant by the owner .

as between landlordand tenant of allsums payable for

or reduced,the sum so made payable as rentshallbe in-
creasedor reducedas the casemay be, by the amount
of every such increaseor reductionin the sum payable
by the landlordforratesin respectof such premises and
attributableto the periodduring which such rentaccrued
and where any such rent ismade payable fora periodor
periodsoflessthan one year,theproperproportionofsuch
increaseor reductionshallbe paid or allowed,as the case
may require, on the occasionof each payment of rent.
Any such increasedor reduced rent shallbe recoverable
in the same manner as the rentreservedby the contract
of tenancy. Provided that for the purposes of the
summary recovery of possessionof any such premises
under the provisionsof sectionfifteenof the Summary
Jurisdiction(Ireland) Act , 1851,the amount of the rent
shallbe deemed tobetheamount computed by deducting
the amount of the ratesfrom the totalsum payable in
respectof rent.
(e) In every contract of tenancy made afterthe
passingof thisAct in respectof any premises to which
sub-section(1) of thissectionappliesany rentthereby
reservedshallbe deemed to be inclusiveofrates,unlessa
contrary intentionshallappear from such contract.

CHAPTER II .
An Act to simplifythe Collectionand Recovery of
Rates in the Urban DistrictofNewry ,and to
authorize the closing of a street in the said
Urban District,and forother purposes.
: [31stMay ,1927.]
WHEREAS the Town of Newry is an Urban
Districtsubjectto the Acts relatingto such Districtsin
Northern Irelandand the Urban DistrictCouncilofNewry
(inthisAct calledthe Council) arethe Urban Sanitary
Authority forthe saidDistrict.
And whereas the expenses of the Council whether
as an Urban Districtor SanitaryAuthority are payable
out ofthe Poor rate,the ConsolidatedTown rate,and the
Water rate .
And whereas itisexpedientthat the owner instead
ofthe occupiershould be liableforand ratedto the Poor
rate, the Consolidated Town rate and the Water rate in
respectof the hereditamentsspecifiedin thisAct.
And whereas itisexpedientthat the Councilshould
be authorisedto closethe Streetin thisAct mentioned,
and to exercise in relation to such Street when closed the
powers in thisAct conferred.
And whereas it is expedient that the other pro
visionsin this Act contained should be enacted ,
And whereas the objects aforesaid cannot be
obtained without the Authority of Parliament.
And whereas in relationto the promotion of the
BillforthisAct the requirementsof the Borough Funds
(Ireland) Act , 1888, have been observed.

200 [Ch .ii.] Newry Urban DistrictCouncil [17 & 18 GEO .5.]
Act (Northern Ireland), 1927 .

That itmay BE ENACTED AND BE IT ENACTED by

as follows(that isto say):-
Short title.
Act divided

tion of
Terms .
PART I. PRELIMINARY .
1. This Act may be cited as the Newry Urban
DistrictCouncilAct (Northern Ireland), 1927.
2. This Act is divided into Parts as follows :-
Part I.- Preliminary.
Part II.--Recovery of Rates.
Part III.- Liabilityof Owner for Rates in
Certain Cases .
Part IV .- Power to the Councilto closeup
a Certain Street .

PART II.- RECOVERY OF RATES .
4. The Poor rate the Consolidated Town rate and the
Water rate may be demanded togetherin one Demand
Note and shall be recoverable in one sum and all the
enactments relatingto the apportionment and recovery
of the Poor rate which are in force at the commencement
ofthisAct shallsubjectto the provisionsofthisAct apply
to the recovery of the ConsolidatedTown rate and the
Water rate. Every Demand Note shallspecifythe
amount in the pound required for the Poor rate the
ConsolidatedTown rateand the Water raterespectively.

CHAPTER iii.
An Act to transferfrom the CarrickfergusHarbour
Commissioners to the Urban District Council
of Carrickfergusthe Harbour of Carrickfergus,
and all other property of the Carrickfergus
Harbour Commissioners ,and to conferpower on
the Urban District Council of Carrickfergus to
execute certain works and to make certain rail-
ways at the said Harbour , and to work ,use,
maintain, and repair the said harbour works
and railways, and to levy tollsfor the use
thereof,and to borrow ten thousand pounds and
to secure repayment thereof by mortgage or
charge and forother purposes.
[31stMay ,1927.]

WHEREAS by the CarrickfergusHarbour Order,
1862, the Municipal Commissioners of the Borough of
Carrickferguswere incorporatedby the name of the
CarrickfergusHarbour Commissioners, and were em-
powered to take and hold land and otherpropertyforthe
purposesof the Order, and the CarrickfergusHarbour
Commissioners were thereby empowered to borrow at
interesta sum or sums not exceeding six thousand
pounds .
And whereas by two Indentures, each dated the
7th day ofMay ,1863,the MunicipalCommissionersofthe
Borough ofCarrickfergusconveyedto the Carrickfergus
Harbour Commissioners the Harbour of Carrickfergus
and the seashoreoppositethereto, and the customs and
shippingdues leviableby the MunicipalCommissioners.
And whereas by the CarrickfergusHarbour Order,
1865, the CarrickfergusHarbour Commissioners were
empowered to borrow at interestsums not exceedingin
the whole eightthousand pounds .
And whereas by the CarrickfergusHarbour Order,
1875, the CarrickfergusHarbour Commissioners were
empowered to borrow such furthersums not exceeding
tenthousand pounds asmight be requiredforthepurposes
of the works thereby authorised.
And whereasby the CarrickfergusHarbour Act,
1880, the Municipal Commissioners of the Borough of
Carrickferguswere empowered, with the consentof the
Commissioners of Her Majesty'sTreasury, and subject
to the provisionsof the Municipal CorporationActs as
to mortgages of the Municipalproperty,to mortgage the
Municipal property forsecuringrepayment with interest
of money borrowed by the CarrickfergusHarbour Com-
missioners under the CarrickfergusHarbour Orders,
1862, 1865 and 1875.
And whereas the CarrickfergusHarbour Com-
missionersin exerciseof theirpowers under the Carrick-
fergusHarbour Orders1862, 1865 and 1875, borrowed
from the Commissioners of Public Works in Ireland the
sum of twelve thousand pounds .
And whereas by Indenture dated the 5th day of
May , 1881, the CarrickfergusHarbour Commissioners,

CHAPTER IV .
An Act to empower the Coleraine Harbour Com-
missioners to construct works to improve the
navigation of the River Bann , and for other
purposes . [31st May , 1927.]
WHEREAS by the River Bann NavigationAct,
1879 (hereinafterreferredto as " the Act of 1879 "),the

## Page 231

[17 & 18 GEO .5.] RiverBann NavigationAct [Ch .iv.] 225
(NorthernIreland),1927.
ColeraineHarbour Commissioners (hereinafterreferredto as " the Commissioners ")were constitutedand incor-
porated and were authorised to construct works and
exercisepowers for the improvement and controlof the
River Bann within the limits therein described and for
such other purposes as are thereinset forth;
A.D. 1927 .
And whereasby the Act of 1879 allthe property,
rights, and privilegespreviouslyvested in and enjoyed
and exerciseableby the Colerainetown Commissioners
pursuant to the River Bann NavigationAct ,1863,in and
over the River Bann within the said limits were transferred
to the Commissioners ;
And whereas by the Act of 1879 the Commissioners
were empowered to borrow money to the extent therein
specifiedand to securethe moneys so borrowed by mort-
gage on " the River Bann Fund ," which the Commis-
sionerswere requiredby the saidAct to setup and to
which they were requiredto carrythesums of money and
income in the said Act mentioned ;
And whereas the Commissioners are executingthe
powersoftheAct of 1879 and have constructedvarious
works and borrowed varioussums of money thereunder;
And whereas the sums now owing by the Com-
missionerson mortgage of the River Bann Fund amount
to three thousand seven hundred and ninety-seven
pounds ,whereof one thousand nine hundred and eighty-
seven pounds isowing in respectof moneys borrowed by
the Commissioners under the powers of the Act of 1879,
and the remainingone thousandeighthundred and tenpounds is owing in respectof mortgages known as " B
Mortgages " createdby the saidColerainetown commis-
sioners and transferred to the Commissioners under the
Act of 1879 .
And whereas by the River Bann Navigation Act ,
1885 (hereinafterreferredto as " the Act of 1885 "),the
Commissioners were empowered to make and maintain
certainrailways and to borrow moneys for the con-
structionthereofand were requiredto carry allrevenue
from such railwaysand from chargesforthe use of cranes
on theirwharves to a separate fund to be calledthe Bann
Railway Revenue Fund and were alsorequiredto carry
all borrowed moneys and other receiptsof a capital
nature in relationto the said railwaysto a fund to be

## Page 232

226 [Ch.iv.] RiverBann NavigationAct [17 & 18 GEO .5.]
A.D. 1927 .
(NorthernIreland),1927.
calledthe Bann Railway CapitalFund ,and itwas pro-
vided that allexpenses of the Commissioners for or in
relationto the executionofthe powers of theAct of 1885
inrelationto the saidrailwaysand cranesshould be paid
as to chargeson capitalout of the Bann Railway Capital
Fund and as to chargeson revenue out of the Bann
Railway Revenue Fund and thatthe saidfunds shouldbe
wholly distinctfrom the River Bann Fund ,and should
not be liableto any debts secured on or chargeable
againstthat fund ;
And whereas by the Act of 1885 the Commissioners
were authorisedto borrow moneys on the securityof the
Bann Railway Revenue Fund and the Commissioners
were empowered to includeby way of additionalor
collateralsecurityinthesecurityforsuchloansany surplus
revenue of the River Bann Fund but the power to give
such additionalor collateralsecurityhas not in fact
been exercised;
And whereas forthebetterprotectionofthe channel
of the said River Bann and the navigationthereofthe
Commissionersinpursuanceof thepowers of theAct of
1879 and soon afterthe passingthereofconstructedtwo
piersat the mouth of the saidRiver,one on eithersideof
the channel thereof, and they alsoat a laterdate con-
structeda trainingbank in the leftor south-west sideof
the riveradjacentto the pieron that side;
And whereas the said piers have been partially
broken down by heavy seasor othercausesand are now
in a partiallyruined conditionso that the sea washes
over them ,and the saidtrainingbank isnot placed in a
suitablepositionfor guiding the current of the river
satisfactorilybetween the saidpiers,and itisexpedient
that the Commissioners should be empowered to recon-
structthe saidpiersand trainingbank in the positions
and in the manner by thisAct authorisedand in con-
nectiontherewithand forthe purposesthereofto acquire
lands, borrow money , and exerciseother powers as in
thisAct provided.
And whereas provisionwas made by the Act of
1879 for enablingthe Commissioners in the case of the
River Bann Fund proving insufficientforpayment in full
of intereston mortgages and certainotherchargesunder
thatAct to make requisitionsupon the Colerainetown

NavigationAct (NorthernIreland), 1927.

may together be cited as the River Bann Navigation
Acts , 1879 to 1927 .
